N) The So What:	At a time when all the investments philanthropy has made in things like public education, early childhood, criminal justice, healthcare, immigration, etc., now is NOT the time to fall back on that myth that foundations can't support lobbying or advocacy.
M)	Generally, under an expense based limit like a 501h election, orgs have more room to move.		The expenditure limit is clearer.
L)	As an advocate a community foundation CAN do both direct and grassroots lobbying up to their IRS limit.		Y'all can't go over.		What this means: a community foundation can act like a grantmaker AND a nonprofit, giving it more advocacy capacity.		(Hint: solicit community fdns)
K)	Community foundations cannot 		üíÄ conduct or fund electioneering activity		üíÄ exceed its lobbying limits (either 'insubstantial' standard or the 501h limit)
J)	Rules for Community Foundations		You can:	ü§î give gen ops support to orgs that lobby	ü§î make project specific grants for projects that include lobbying	ü§îmake grants that support advocacy		Lookit all you can do!!
I)	Back to the rules:		Private foundations MAY NOT		üíÄearmark grants specifically for lobbying		üíÄfund political campaign/electioneering activity		Rally against untested census questions yes	Rally for a candidate no
H)	Those certain steps are usually around building a wall around the direct lobbying portion of the grantee activity thru their budget.		You can find the grantee's **entire project** as long as they cover the direct lobbying expenses.		Think about that.
G)	Basic rules for private foundations:		ü§îYou can give gen ops to orgs that lobby	ü§îYou can give project specific grants to orgs that INCLUDE lobbying as long as certain steps are taken	ü§îMake grants to support lobbying
F)	All of that is advocacy.	And it's allowed.	For foundations to fund and nonprofits to do.
